  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12281829384078254033">You remember Hannibal Lecter: gentleman. genius. cannibal.<br /><br />Seven years have passed since Dr. Lecter escaped from custody. And for seven years he's been at large, free to savor the scents, the essences, of an unguarded world. But intruders have entered Dr. Lecter's sanctuary, piercing his new identity, sensing the evil that surrounds him. For the multimillionaire Hannibal left maimed, for a corrupt Italian policeman. and for FBI agent Clarice Starling, who once stood before Lecter and who has never been the same, the hunt for Hannibal Lecter has begun. All of them, in their separate ways, want to find Dr. Lecter. And all three will get their wish. But only one will live long enough to savor the reward...</span>

<div class="answererUserIcon">
<a href="/user/show/6422991-she-m" class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto"><img src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/users/1316809017i/6422991._UY100_CR12,0,100,100_.jpg" alt="" /></a>
</div>
<div class="communityAnswerTextContainer">
<span class="communityAnswererName">
<a href="/user/show/6422991-she-m">She' M</a>
</span>
<span class="communityAnswerText">
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I think quite a bit of the end can be confusing - after Clarice comes to, I wasn't quite sure what was going on with her character, it becomes<a href="#" class="jsShow showAction">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I think quite a bit of the end can be confusing - after Clarice comes to, I wasn't quite sure what was going on with her character, it becomes increasingly clear that hypnosis and drugs were involved. But for me there was still a question of what was drug induced and what wasn't and does this entirely explain her behavior....<br />And WTF was up with that "making space for Mischa" bull???<br />Either way, the ending was kind of cheap. It would've made more sense if he ate her eventually<a href="#" class="jsHide hideAction">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>

    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_4939679">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/4939679" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/275001-peggy" class="left imgcol" title="Peggy"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1187021327p2/275001.jpg" alt="Peggy" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/4939679?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 22, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/275001-peggy" class="user" title="Peggy">Peggy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer4939679">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14182342841306340494">Okay, let me confess up front: I loved <em>Red Dragon</em> and <em>The Silence of the Lambs</em>. <strong>Loved</strong> them. I enjoyed the movies, too: the movie version of <em>Silence of the Lambs</em> scared the pee out of me, and even so, I didn’t want it to end. So, long years later when I finally got hold of a copy of <em>Hannibal</em>, I really, really, wanted to love it, too.<br /><br />But I didn’t.<br /><br />Well, that’s not entirely true. If I pretend that this wasn’t a sequel about characters I already know, then I can find some bright spots. The book has s</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14182342841306340494">Okay, let me confess up front: I loved <em>Red Dragon</em> and <em>The Silence of the Lambs</em>. <strong>Loved</strong> them. I enjoyed the movies, too: the movie version of <em>Silence of the Lambs</em> scared the pee out of me, and even so, I didn’t want it to end. So, long years later when I finally got hold of a copy of <em>Hannibal</em>, I really, really, wanted to love it, too.<br /><br />But I didn’t.<br /><br />Well, that’s not entirely true. If I pretend that this wasn’t a sequel about characters I already know, then I can find some bright spots. The book has some fantastic descriptions of Italy. There are certainly some creepy scenes that gave me the shivers. I was fascinated by the concept of the memory cathedral. And I felt terribly bad for poor Clarice as her world crumbled in around her. The problem is, none of the characters seem remotely connected to the folks we met before.<br /><br />Hannibal Lecter, an enigma in previous installments, now has a background. It’s tragic and horrifying, but is it enough to form the Hannibal we all know? Maybe. But even if it is, do we really have to know the details of why Lecter is who he is? I’m not convinced that this information makes him a more compelling character.<br /><br />Clarice Starling, whose wagon was hitched to a rising star at the end of Silence, is on the verge of being pushed out of the FBI. She has been overlooked again and again for promotion and is reduced to being scapegoated by talentless superiors.<br /><br />Jack Crawford, a hero and mentor in the previous books, is now (for the short time he appears here) a liability.<br /><br />I understand that people change, but come on. So what happened? What changed between the publication of <em>The Silence of the Lambs</em> and the publication of <em>Hannibal</em>? Well, what changed was the character of Hannibal Lecter. In both <em>Red Dragon</em> and <em>The Silence of the Lambs</em>, Hannibal was a minor (though quite compelling) character. Harris went to great pains to point out that, although clever and extremely cunning, Lecter was not omniscient. There was always an explanation as to how he knew the things he did, and Crawford was equally clever at figuring it out. Enter Jonathan Demme.<br /><br />When Jonathan Demme made the movie version of <em>Silence</em>, he said that he wanted the audience to believe that Lecter was the smartest man alive. It didn’t matter how he knew the things he did—he just <strong>knew</strong>. And to the credit of both Demme and Anthony Hopkins, it worked. The movie firmly established Lecter’s genius, and in the context of the film, it was brilliant: you never have to explain how Lecter gets his information, and his outrageous escape becomes plausible. Besides, the smarter Lecter is the more the audience worries about Clarice. Hopkins’ performance firmly established a picture in our minds of who Lecter was and how he worked.<br /><br />Enter Thomas Harris, trying to write a sequel to a phenomenally popular book, which was also a hugely successful movie. Now everyone thought of Anthony Hopkins when they thought of Hannibal Lecter, and they believed he was the smartest psycho alive. Instead of writing about his own Hannibal, he tried to write about the Demme/Hopkins Hannibal, and that just didn’t leave him anyplace to go but over the top, which is a crying shame. The book collapses under the sheer magnitude of what we are expected to accept about these characters and where they end up. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14182342841306340494">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_2896387">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2896387" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/176618-noiresque" class="left imgcol" title="Noiresque"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1196363474p2/176618.jpg" alt="Noiresque" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/2896387?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 13, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/176618-noiresque" class="user" title="Noiresque">Noiresque</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/966744.Hannibal" title="Hardcover 9780385299299" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer2896387">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5847698997381764600">I have a theory about this horrible book.<br /><br />Both <a title=" Red Dragon" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Red%20Dragon"> Red Dragon</a> and <a title=" The Silence of the Lambs" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20The%20Silence%20of%20the%20Lambs"> The Silence of the Lambs</a> are formidable pieces of pop fiction. They are well-written thrillers with great descriptions and characters. They were both adapted into great movies. They made <a title=" Thomas Harris" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Thomas%20Harris"> Thomas Harris</a> a very rich man.<br /><br />I think Mr. Harris made a bet, maybe with a friend or just to himself. He knew that his next novel would be snapped up for big bucks for the screen rights. He knew he would not get any control over the script. So he dec</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5847698997381764600">I have a theory about this horrible book.<br /><br />Both <a title=" Red Dragon" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Red%20Dragon"> Red Dragon</a> and <a title=" The Silence of the Lambs" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20The%20Silence%20of%20the%20Lambs"> The Silence of the Lambs</a> are formidable pieces of pop fiction. They are well-written thrillers with great descriptions and characters. They were both adapted into great movies. They made <a title=" Thomas Harris" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Thomas%20Harris"> Thomas Harris</a> a very rich man.<br /><br />I think Mr. Harris made a bet, maybe with a friend or just to himself. He knew that his next novel would be snapped up for big bucks for the screen rights. He knew he would not get any control over the script. So he decided to write a book that would basically be un-filmable. It would be so preposterous, such dreck, that it would drive the screenwriters crazy. And Mr. Harris would be laughing all the way to the bank.<br /><br />This theory makes it possible to think that Thomas Harris is talented. There are other theories that eliminate that possibility. Of course, the publication of <a title=" Hannibal Rising" href="https://www.goodreads.com/search/search?q=%20Hannibal%20Rising"> Hannibal Rising</a> kind of shoot my theory all to hell.<br /><br />I can't believe I was so excited about this book that I rushed out to buy it in hardcover. Ugh. I sold it to a used bookstore at the first opportunity. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5847698997381764600">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_75719188">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/75719188" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2874565-sufferingbruin" class="left imgcol" title="Sufferingbruin"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/u_50x66-632230dc9882b4352d753eedf9396530.png" alt="Sufferingbruin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/75719188?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 03, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2874565-sufferingbruin" class="user" title="Sufferingbruin">Sufferingbruin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer75719188">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9674763135041627199">Lord, what an awful book. Awash in mediocrity from first page to last. It has mediocre characters (the same which were so captivating in "Silence of the Lambs"), mediocre dialogue, mediocre scenery, virtually no suspense (but a plethora of pointlessly putrid acts), and a meandering narrative that often lacks consistency of time and place. "Hannibal" does not induce fear or revulsion so much as groans and guffaws. But don't worry: there's a bleeding HIV-postiive woman holding a baby whose last li</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9674763135041627199">Lord, what an awful book. Awash in mediocrity from first page to last. It has mediocre characters (the same which were so captivating in "Silence of the Lambs"), mediocre dialogue, mediocre scenery, virtually no suspense (but a plethora of pointlessly putrid acts), and a meandering narrative that often lacks consistency of time and place. "Hannibal" does not induce fear or revulsion so much as groans and guffaws. But don't worry: there's a bleeding HIV-postiive woman holding a baby whose last line is "let's swap fluids, bitch" before she's shot to death mid-crime. There are man eating pigs who are intended to be filmed in the act by people from the porn industry, at the behest of a sub-villain recovering from having his face chewed up by dogs. Thankfully, he gets by with having the tears of children put into his IV. No, that last sentence was not a joke. And of course, our two rivals are back.<br /><br />Clarice Starling gets the worst of it in "Hannibal". She has lost all trace of vulnerability and trepidation so there's nothing to overcome. In other words, she's lost what made her human in the previous book. Here, she's wizened super-woman; so cynical, so powerful and of course, distant. We don't know why she is all of these things and Harris doesn't seem to care. There are hints of being passed over at the agency and we can guess from her dour persona that Special Agent Starling is weary of the world but these are only guesses; nothing Clarice says or does leads to inferences one way or the other because it's her turn to play second fiddle. <br /><br />Harris' previous efforts, "Red Dragon" and especially "Silence of the Lambs" are both terrific. In both, Lecter plays a role (small in "Dragon" and of course, much larger in "Lambs") but supporting roles. "Red Dragon" explored profiling, a valuable but punishing trade. How much damage can happen when you take on the mind of a killer to catch the killer? Will Graham finds out in a brief visit to Lecter, ostensibly to get information on another serial killer when Lecter memorably calls him out: "You came back to get the smell back, didn't you? Smell yourself." Harris went further with "Lambs", with a myriad of themes, all of them intriguing, all of them meticulously developed. Which brings us to "Hannibal" and a crucial question after a painful week of reading: What is the theme here? Lecter is the unquestioned star of the show but what does Lecter have to tell us? I'm at a loss. We know he insists on only the best material accoutrements (to borrow a phrase from our sociopath)--the best food, the best cars and for heaven's sake, the best clothes. He travels the world, sniffing at the coarseness of his fellow citizens when he's not killing them. So Harris, in his infinite wisdom, has made Lecter a snob whose only relief from the utter pain of flying coach (oh, the humanity) is the foie de gras he sneaks on board. <br /><br />It takes awhile but the two engage. By that time, the reader is either beaten into submission or baffled as to why another page is to be turned. If--and it's a big if--reading continues, there is a conclusion so laugh-out-loud ridiculous one has to wonder about Harris' true intent. The best that can be said is that he wants to wash his hands of the whole enterprise. If so, mission accomplished. There is literally nowhere left for either to go, no worlds left to conquer though the world they inhabit doesn't resemble anything like the one we are living in. <br /><br />Shorter review: this is a book that makes you wish a zero star rating was possible. <br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9674763135041627199">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_510502630">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/510502630" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/16182382-chris-shepherdson" class="left imgcol" title="Chris Shepherdson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1375618518p2/16182382.jpg" alt="Chris Shepherdson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/510502630?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 24, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/16182382-chris-shepherdson" class="user" title="Chris Shepherdson">Chris Shepherdson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer510502630">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15046082561611374643">When Thomas Harris created the infamous Hannibal Lector in Red Dragon he couldn't have known the influence that character would have on crime fiction for the next decade. By the time he came to write Hannibal, ten years after his previous book, The Silence of The Lambs, he must have felt some serious pressure. The fact that Hannibal is the book it is, when written under these circumstances, makes it all the more remarkable.<br />To call it a crime novel is doing it a grave injustice and reading it as</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText15046082561611374643">When Thomas Harris created the infamous Hannibal Lector in Red Dragon he couldn't have known the influence that character would have on crime fiction for the next decade. By the time he came to write Hannibal, ten years after his previous book, The Silence of The Lambs, he must have felt some serious pressure. The fact that Hannibal is the book it is, when written under these circumstances, makes it all the more remarkable.<br />To call it a crime novel is doing it a grave injustice and reading it as such will also leave the reader disappointed. This book sits closer to Stoker's Dracula or Shelly's Frankenstein than the serial killer fare of Michael Connelly. Treat this book more as gothic fairytale and you won't be disappointed. <br />The greatest triumph of The Silence of The Lambs is, as iconic as the film version is, it scarecely registers as you read the book. You are taken into another world and any thought of Jodie Foster and Anthony Hopkins are gone. The same is true of Hannibal, and then some.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="15046082561611374643">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/205023629?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 03, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6197685-stargirl" class="user" title="Stargirl">Stargirl</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer205023629">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer818715651920457182">Oh that ending. Sublime. <br /><br />Gothic horror detective chase story, blends genres with great ease, affirming Harris as a master storyteller- as if we didn't already know. Don't go in expecting another Red Dragon or Silence of the Lambs. This is a much bigger, far darker experience. It's all in the title people. Silence was the story of Clarice Starling, so there is a lot of hope and innocence to it. This one, is about the dark side of her character- and of that awful/awesome Doctor Mr Lecter himself.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText818715651920457182">Oh that ending. Sublime. <br /><br />Gothic horror detective chase story, blends genres with great ease, affirming Harris as a master storyteller- as if we didn't already know. Don't go in expecting another Red Dragon or Silence of the Lambs. This is a much bigger, far darker experience. It's all in the title people. Silence was the story of Clarice Starling, so there is a lot of hope and innocence to it. This one, is about the dark side of her character- and of that awful/awesome Doctor Mr Lecter himself. <br /><br />A decadent spiral into madness and obliteration. A glimpse into hell. <br /><br />The quality of the writing is of the highest order, blurring the lines between popular fiction and literature. <br /><br />Ingenious and over the top, a true sequel that shows no mercy. <br /><br />And the ending... Sweet God. It really puts the reader in his/her place, reminding you that you have no control over the characters you read. The author is in charge and he will take you into places, dragging and screaming, that you don't want to know. Harris is James Gumb from Silence of the Lambs and this book is the pit he threw Catherine Martin into. Only she escaped . . . </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_14610767">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/14610767" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/862037-james" class="left imgcol" title="James"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442474053p2/862037.jpg" alt="James" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/14610767?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Feb 05, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/862037-james" class="user" title="James">James</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>

          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">I wouldn't</span></div>

        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer14610767">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8787924427416116959">The book starts off wonderfully with Harris's visualization; you can see everything you read. There are complex characters introduced and of course a wicked weave between them. He shows the master insanity of Hannibal with his elaborate set-ups for escape from not only Starling but from a vile creature named Verger who sets out to seek revenge on the good doctor. And you are eating this up the whole time, because it seems that Harris is once again quite the masterful story teller. But then you g</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText8787924427416116959">The book starts off wonderfully with Harris's visualization; you can see everything you read. There are complex characters introduced and of course a wicked weave between them. He shows the master insanity of Hannibal with his elaborate set-ups for escape from not only Starling but from a vile creature named Verger who sets out to seek revenge on the good doctor. And you are eating this up the whole time, because it seems that Harris is once again quite the masterful story teller. But then you get to the last few chapters. <br />The best way I can describe it is it seems like he took his time and thought out every little detail like it was the master term paper. But then all of a sudden he realizes he doesn't have the time needed to finish it so he rushes it and throws an ending together. It was almost like to different authors. And of the ending! And what he does with Clarice! I was put off by the whole book in a matter of a few thousand words.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="8787924427416116959">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_159781196">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/159781196" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite" class="left imgcol" title="Erin (Paperbackstash) *Book Hoarders Unite!*"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1448768136p2/3048260.jpg" alt="Erin (Paperbackstash) *Book Hoarders Unite!*" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/159781196?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 29, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite" class="user" title="Erin (Paperbackstash) *Book Hoarders Unite!*">Erin (Paperbackstash) *Book Hoarders Unite!*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite?shelf=a-own-book-form" class="actionLinkLite">a-own-book-form</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite?shelf=thrillers-susp" class="actionLinkLite">thrillers-susp</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite?shelf=serial-killer" class="actionLinkLite">serial-killer</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite?shelf=5-star" class="actionLinkLite">5-star</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/3048260-erin-paperbackstash-book-hoarders-unite?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer159781196">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13356634046180629704">**Note - After my re-read on 3/24/15, have bumped from four to five stars and edited review a little. *<br /><br />I read the four books in order of sequence, not publication, ending with Hannibal. I'm not sure if it was following them in order or my mood, but I was more enamored this time around. It's turned out to be my favorite in the series. I know this isn't the popular opinion, but I think Harris did a brilliant job wrapping up the series.<br /><br />The plot is as diabolical as Silence of the Lambs was, this tim</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13356634046180629704">**Note - After my re-read on 3/24/15, have bumped from four to five stars and edited review a little. *<br /><br />I read the four books in order of sequence, not publication, ending with Hannibal. I'm not sure if it was following them in order or my mood, but I was more enamored this time around. It's turned out to be my favorite in the series. I know this isn't the popular opinion, but I think Harris did a brilliant job wrapping up the series.<br /><br />The plot is as diabolical as Silence of the Lambs was, this time concentrating more on Clarice and Hannibal’s “relationship.” Hannibal Lecter is explored a lot more through internal dialogue; I learned a about his though process (disturbing as it was). I sat back in awe at his life experiences, his true motivations, and the odd little ‘room in his mind.’ The person inside of me interested in psychology found his detachment methods fascinating. His motivations, while not morally just, were made clearer by seeing it through his point of view. While I’d never agree with his actions, it was still better than being left in the dark. As always, I loved being in Clarices’ head. She’s morally righteous, determined, hard working, loyal and honest;­ the change she went through nearly stopped my breath.<br /><br />As mentioned before with the story, I DID lose interest after the beginning to a little after the center. The pacing was even during that time, but the material just didn’t keep my eyes wandering. I'm referring to that stint in Italy, which dulled a little and I wish Harris had spent a little less time in that section.<br /><br />Harris’s style, particularly when focusing on Lecter and Sterling, was intense and clever. His wording was sophisticated and drama-filled, sounding disturbing when it should have been. His use of dialogue was realistic, his action scenes well sketched so that the most damage that could be done to my nerves was. His sense of irony with plot really sang through.<br /><br />The ending of Hannibal is one of the most powerful I’ve ever read. I literally sat back and had to think for over an hour afterward…seriously. Not many books shake me up like that at the end; the last was a few years back by Sidney Sheldon. The novel wrap up was different than it’s cinema relative; don’t go in expected the same thing you see on screen, because it WONT HAPPEN.<br /><br />I wasn’t sure what emotion was appropriate when I read the finale. Mainly I was disturbed, as well as saddened, but in a strange, strange, strange, place deep inside, I was also pleased. (!) I don’t know what this says about ME, but the bottom line is Harris did his job so well with the last scenes, he almost did it a little ‘too’ well.<br /><br />It ties into the becoming, that bizarre act of transformation focused on by Jame Gumb, made famous in the series most famous work, Silence of the Lamb. To wrap up the series on that note is genius in its circular resolution. What Clarice revealed about herself, the price she paid as she sought to stop a madman from transforming an innocent woman into his vision of himself is now transferred to the second madman, the one who helped her stop the first.<br /><br />I couldn’t decide whether I should give it a four or a five rating; because of the middle lagging, I was going to settle on a four, but because of the powerful influence the ending had (it’s hard to impress me on THAT level), I just have to give it a five. It more than made up for its faults.<br /><br />Read Hannibal and experience the trauma for yourself. This novel doesn’t hesitate to psychologically assault its reader.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13356634046180629704">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_26434188">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/26434188" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1269587-rosie" class="left imgcol" title="Rosie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1382121278p2/1269587.jpg" alt="Rosie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/26434188?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 12, 2008</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1269587-rosie" class="user" title="Rosie">Rosie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1269587-rosie?shelf=books-i-own" class="actionLinkLite">books-i-own</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/1269587-rosie?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer26434188">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16522394998984575609">I was obviously relishing my next installment in the world of Clarice Starling and Dr Hannibal Lecter. The book opens explosively with dramatic happenings, despite Starling's FBI career being a slight anti-climax due to influences from former enemies. Again, I'd seen the film before I read the book and so most of the major plot occurences I was already aware of, but there are more differences between the two Hannibal medias than in the films of Harris' previous two novels. The film had the advan</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16522394998984575609">I was obviously relishing my next installment in the world of Clarice Starling and Dr Hannibal Lecter. The book opens explosively with dramatic happenings, despite Starling's FBI career being a slight anti-climax due to influences from former enemies. Again, I'd seen the film before I read the book and so most of the major plot occurences I was already aware of, but there are more differences between the two Hannibal medias than in the films of Harris' previous two novels. The film had the advantage of being able to <em>show</em> us Mason Verger's appearance in all his glory, and yet - possibly in the attempt to demonize Hannibal Lecter further - didn't reveal the information from the book which showed Mason was always ugly, faceless or not. The book offers more insight into Dr Lecter's psyche as well as Clarice's, and yet neither are open pages. The reason that I decided to read this series was because the film Hannibal was tragically haunting near the end, and so it would be my luck that the end is where the two medias differ extremely. Although, it was intriguing to see the extra interactions between such complex characters, it was almost as if I was enjoying the insight of where we were at, without really knowing how we got there. Nearer the end I almost felt as though Clarice was a completely different character than what I had originally thought. Rather ironic, that the sane character is the one who confused me, whilst I could count on Dr Lecter to be mysteriously predictable, but not by any normal standards. Thomas Harris writes directly to the reader, acknowledging we are not part of the happenings and invites us to tour silently the halls of his characters' minds and abodes, yet he also writes from within such characters as they endure terrifying and confusing events. We live through the most meaningful parts of their lives and yet by the end, neither of the main characters are open books to us. I think the revelations of Dr Lecter's past experiences almost made him seem weaker to me, and that's not what I wanted from a book of his namesake. I wasn't entirely pleased at Dr Lecter's thoughts following hypothesis made by Stephen Hawking, as I'd always held the thought that despite the murders and cannibalism he was actually sane, which would be most disturbing of all, and yet these thoughts seemed to hint otherwise. As always, I am a romantic and yet I feel the film's ending was how it should have ended - for two characters such as they, only a tragic parting seemed befitting. Fantastically written, Harris mixes the vulgar and the culturally fanciful at every turn. I read the book to try and understand the characters better, and instead I think I may have confused myself further. The only constant is the two main characters, Clarice Starling and Hannibal Lecter, and the feelings, thoughts and actions which occur when their paths collide. I doubt there is anyone who wouldn't be fascinated the crackling sexual and mental tension between Starling and Lecter, as they are inevitably consumed by thoughts of each other.<br /><br />I enjoyed this trilogy, through The Dragon and Buffalo Bill, through Will Graham's plight and from Clarice Starling's first encounter with Dr Hannibal Lecter through to the point of no return. Fascinating reading, and although I think Hannibal maybe wasn't the best climax to Silence of the Lambs (I agree with others about the changes in characters, and the difference in...quality, maybe?) I'm sure this will still play on my mind in years to come.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16522394998984575609">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_224699242">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/224699242" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2716255-andrew-breslin" class="left imgcol" title="Andrew Breslin"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1442476483p2/2716255.jpg" alt="Andrew Breslin" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/224699242?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 18, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2716255-andrew-breslin" class="user" title="Andrew Breslin">Andrew Breslin</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer224699242">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11962503764018561489">I've been openly endorsing a lot of cannibalism lately, what with my "Eat the Rich" sign down at the ongoing occupy Philadelphia event up the street. As far as a strategy for revolutionary change and general economic improvement, I'm not sure it will work, but it couldn't possibly be any less effective than supply-side economics, and would be much more fun. <br /><br />Hannibal Lecter is, arguably, literature's most beloved cannibal. I say "arguably" only because I want to start an argument so I'll have mor</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11962503764018561489">I've been openly endorsing a lot of cannibalism lately, what with my "Eat the Rich" sign down at the ongoing occupy Philadelphia event up the street. As far as a strategy for revolutionary change and general economic improvement, I'm not sure it will work, but it couldn't possibly be any less effective than supply-side economics, and would be much more fun. <br /><br />Hannibal Lecter is, arguably, literature's most beloved cannibal. I say "arguably" only because I want to start an argument so I'll have more justification for eating someone. But really, he's pretty much it, and Harris does a great job making him both terrifying and likable. You get a little bit more inside the head of the good doctor than in <em>Silence of the Lambs</em>, and who wouldn't want to be inside that head? One might be tempted to question the general mental state of an author who makes us root for a sociopathic devourer of human flesh. Not me, though, I hasten to point out, and also state for the record my absolutely disgusting personal hygiene and general lack of savoriness. <br /><br />This a good thriller, and you might even pick up a few culinary tips along the way. I don't have much more to say about it so instead: some cannibal jokes:<br /><br />Did you hear about the cannibal who arrived late for dinner? <br /><br />He got the cold shoulder.<br /><br />........<br /><br />Two cannibals are having dinner together and talking.<br /><br />"You know," says the first, "I really can't stand my mother-in-law"<br /><br />The second ones shrugs and says "so have the potatoes."<br /><br />.........<br /><br />Why don't cannibals eat comedians?<br /><br />They taste funny.<br /><br />...............<br /><br />Cannibals capture a Frenchman, and Englishman, and a New Yorker. They tell their captives that they are going to be killed and skinned to make canoes, and their innards boiled for stew. The good news is they can choose how they die.<br /><br />"Well, that's a spot of bad luck, isn't it old chap?" muses the Englishman. "well., a pistol I suppose then." They give him a pistol. "God save the queen!" he says, and blows his brains out.<br /><br />"I vill take zee sword, you cannibal pig dogs!" curses the Frenchman. They hand him a sword and he shouts "Vive la France!" before plunging it into his chest.<br /><br />"I'll take a fork," says the New Yorker.<br /><br />So the cannibals hand him a fork, and he starts stabbing himself all over. He stabs all up and down his legs and his arms and his buttocks and his side and his abdomen and his chest. Blood is oozing out of him from a dozen new orifices, and his lungs are collapsing, but with his last dying breath he manages to raise his middle finger and sputter:<br /><br />"So much for your fucking canoe!!"<br /><br /><br />.................<br />Thank, folks. You've been a great audience. I'll be here all week. Tip your waitress. Try the meatloaf. It's excellent. No, really, it tastes fine to me. <br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="11962503764018561489">...more</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5701086-branwen-sedai-of-the-white-ajah" class="user" title="Branwen Sedai *of the White Ajah*">Branwen Sedai *of the White Ajah*</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5701086-branwen-sedai-of-the-white-ajah?shelf=favorites" class="actionLinkLite">favorites</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/5701086-branwen-sedai-of-the-white-ajah?shelf=thriller" class="actionLinkLite">thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer189088952">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1646317168697933471">***Edit: Second time reading it:<br /><br /><em>"You are a warrior, Clarice. The most stable elements appear in the middle of the periodic table, roughly between iron and silver. Between iron and silver. I think that is appropriate for you. Did you ever think, Clarice, why the Philistines don't understand you? It's because you are the answer to Samson's riddle: You are the honey in the lion."</em><br /><br />In this tale of murder and mayhem from the esteemed Thomas Harris, we follow Hannibal Lecter across the globe as he is ru</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1646317168697933471">***Edit: Second time reading it:<br /><br /><em>"You are a warrior, Clarice. The most stable elements appear in the middle of the periodic table, roughly between iron and silver. Between iron and silver. I think that is appropriate for you. Did you ever think, Clarice, why the Philistines don't understand you? It's because you are the answer to Samson's riddle: You are the honey in the lion."</em><br /><br />In this tale of murder and mayhem from the esteemed Thomas Harris, we follow Hannibal Lecter across the globe as he is ruthlessly pursued by Mason Verger in an attempt to exact revenge over a past atrocity. But some monsters are worse than others. And sometimes help comes in the most unlikely of forms...<br /><br />I freaking knew it. I KNEW that I would love this book about a hundred times more the second time around! A lot of that probably has to do with my recent growing (and probably unhealthy?) infatuation with Dr. Hannibal Lecter thanks to the brilliant nbc series. But I also believe that I enjoyed it more because I am more mature this time around and understand the nature of 'monsters' a little better now that I am older and (dare I say it?) a little bit wiser. <br /><br /><em>At last she reached Dr. Lecter's cell. Here she had had the most remarkable encounter of her life. Here she had been startled, shocked, surprised. Here she had heard things about herself so terribly true her heart resounded like a great deep bell. She wanted to go inside. She wanted to go in, wanting it as we want to jump from balconies, as the glint of the rails tempts us when we hear the approaching train...</em><br /><br />The ending sort of repulsed me the first time around. I didn't really understand the relationship between Hannibal and Clarice before, but I think I do now. They understand each other and relate to each other in a way that is unique when compared to the relationships they have with other people. It's terrifying and complicated and beautiful all at the same.<br /><br />This book is very...interesting to say the least! I would definitely recommend giving it a try, even if something like this isn't your normal cup of tea.<br /><br /><br /><em>"Dr. Lecter has perfect manners, not stiff, but easy and elegant. That didn't mean he wouldn't kill me any second if he had the chance-one quality in a person doesn't rule out any other quality. They can exist side by side-the good and the terrible."</em><br /><a rel="nofollow" target="_blank" href="http://s24.photobucket.com/user/renamon_slave/media/tumblr_n5pv1jdZKh1s9c6nao1_500_zps5bcff232.jpg.html">
  <img class="escapedImg" alt=" photo tumblr_n5pv1jdZKh1s9c6nao1_500_zps5bcff232.jpg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1400390538i/9671008._SY540_.jpg" /></a><br /><br /><br />After first reading:<br />I am very conflicted as to how I feel about this book. I almost put it down about halfway through, because I was just so damn bored and disgusted with it. I love Silence of the Lambs, because the intensity of the characters and their encounters is just so amazing. This book (until the last few chapters) seemed to really lack that. But. At the end of the book I really found myself cheering for Hannibal Lector, and when I realized I was doing it I found myself confused. Why would I cheer for a monster? Which then brought into question what a monster truly is. Is Hannibal a monster? Or was it some of the other characters (such as Mason and Krendler) who were corrupt and sadistic? This book really made me question a lot of morals and ethics, which is a good thing because it really made me think about some things I normally wouldn't. So all in all, I definately feel that although this book is no where near as strong as other books by this author, it is still worth reading.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1646317168697933471">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1160453927?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 27, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/8187431-rade" class="user" title="Rade ">Rade </a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/8187431-rade?shelf=reviewed" class="actionLinkLite">reviewed</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1160453927">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer859853219724632119">"is it as good as <em>Red Dragon</em> and <em>The Silence of the Lambs</em>? No...this one is better." - Stephen King<br /><br />Oh put a cork in it, King. I love you but you are not being truthful at all. This book was IMO a giant turd of words. Feel free to disagree. <br /><br />For one, Lecter needs to remain a secondary character, the kind that will offer advice and feed on personal information of the people interviewing him. In this book he is featured a lot more than in other books. He is free but at the same time he is hunted and</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText859853219724632119">"is it as good as <em>Red Dragon</em> and <em>The Silence of the Lambs</em>? No...this one is better." - Stephen King<br /><br />Oh put a cork in it, King. I love you but you are not being truthful at all. This book was IMO a giant turd of words. Feel free to disagree. <br /><br />For one, Lecter needs to remain a secondary character, the kind that will offer advice and feed on personal information of the people interviewing him. In this book he is featured a lot more than in other books. He is free but at the same time he is hunted and he knows exactly who is hunting him. How? No idea. If you say he got enemies, it can be said just about anyone who he saw in his office or otherwise is his enemy. He does not necessarily help people. He points them in a right direction but does not explicitly say what they should do. Most time he enjoys torturing people in any way he wants. He is like a worm burrowing in you, always itching yet you can't scratch it. <br /><br />Two, Mason. A bit of a different character (in his appearance, at least) but his plan with pigs did not interest me one bit. His Roid Rage sister also creeped me out. The whole Italian hunt was rather tedious, going on forever. <br /><br />Three, the length of this book. Clocking over 500 pages, it felt sort of mundane. If I don't care about one character story line which was 1/3 of the book, it is hard for me to love the entire book. It dragged on and I think there was bunch of things that could have eliminated altogether. At least 10 out of the 103 chapters. <br /><br />And four, Starling. Once again she is found in a situation where she acted instinctively, got the job done, and got suspended because it is against regulations or some shit. She is like one of those rogue cop characters from 80s action movies where she plays by her rules and even if she ends up saving lives, her actions are frowned upon because it seems the end NEVER justifies the means. I am still lacking words to understand her actions in the end. I did like the whole eel part though. <br /><br />Do me a favor and just skip this one. Not even close to the first two books and don't listen to King. He can suck it. </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_169797190">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/169797190" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5477163-steve-morgan" class="left imgcol" title="Steve Morgan"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1383841999p2/5477163.jpg" alt="Steve Morgan" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/169797190?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 20, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5477163-steve-morgan" class="user" title="Steve Morgan">Steve Morgan</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer169797190">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1064229477142790172">*CONTAINS SPOILERS &amp; SWEETBREADS*<br />After discovering Harris upon seeing the phenomenal movie 'Manhunter' in the '80s I sought out Red Dragon which was a fantastic and gripping cat &amp; mouse rollercoaster ride. It's follow up was of course Silence Of The Lambs, equally engrossing and with a massively popular movie adaptation to boot. It was therefore such a massive disappointment to read Hannibal, a book I'd waited impatiently for for the best part of a decade. <br />In all honesty I don't think I'</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1064229477142790172">*CONTAINS SPOILERS &amp; SWEETBREADS*<br />After discovering Harris upon seeing the phenomenal movie 'Manhunter' in the '80s I sought out Red Dragon which was a fantastic and gripping cat &amp; mouse rollercoaster ride. It's follow up was of course Silence Of The Lambs, equally engrossing and with a massively popular movie adaptation to boot. It was therefore such a massive disappointment to read Hannibal, a book I'd waited impatiently for for the best part of a decade. <br />In all honesty I don't think I've ever felt so deflated by a book I'd eagerly anticipated. It had nothing to do with my expectations being too high, the simple fact is Harris lost the plot with Hannibal and I'm not sure how or why he could get it so wrong. The story is so absurd and OTT that I even wondered if post-SOTL Harris had started to see the Lecter character as an albatross and wanted to bury it along with the good Doctor's victims. If he did he went about it in the most ridiculous ways imaginable and how he could expect his devoted fans to stomach the climax of the story is totally confusing. <br />For what it's worth my opinion is that the Lecter character worked so wondefully in the first two books because he's used sparingly. A whole book devoted to Lecter takes away a lot of the enigma Harris so brilliantly built around him in Red Dragon &amp; SOTL. <br />But it's not that simple. The tragedy of this book is that Harris takes the story almost into the realms of science fiction. I've certainly read science fiction that was more believable! But the biggest kick in the nuts was the climax, where we're expected to accept that Lecter keeps the now captured Clarice in a constant state of hypnosis, dashes off to South America where she eventually succumbs to her hidden devotion to the cannibal psychopath and they live happily ever after, a future that presumably involves her knitting him cute sweaters while he keeps them well fed in a diet of sweetbreads and brains. Sigh. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1064229477142790172">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_597924189">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/597924189" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4041033-chris" class="left imgcol" title="Chris"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1352438001p2/4041033.jpg" alt="Chris" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/597924189?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 15, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4041033-chris" class="user" title="Chris">Chris</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/17304398-hannibal" title="Audiobook 9781415951415" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer597924189">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1587387201080630965">I am not sure what to say about this book. I really liked it and it is easily a solid 4.5 stars. I will try to break down what I liked and what I was not to fond of that caused this to be less than a 5 star read. I am still just speechless over the whole thing but in a good way. Shocked into silence because of the amazing writing of Thomas Harris is how I feel after finishing this book. <br /><br />This being the third book in the Hannibal Lecter series, I have been enjoying each step. The problem with read</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1587387201080630965">I am not sure what to say about this book. I really liked it and it is easily a solid 4.5 stars. I will try to break down what I liked and what I was not to fond of that caused this to be less than a 5 star read. I am still just speechless over the whole thing but in a good way. Shocked into silence because of the amazing writing of Thomas Harris is how I feel after finishing this book. <br /><br />This being the third book in the Hannibal Lecter series, I have been enjoying each step. The problem with reading them back to back is that I constantly compare them. Red Dragon is still my favorite of the series because the quick pace and amazing intrigue and suspense. This book did come close to that however. The action and characters where exactly what I have come to expect from Thomas Harris. There was just one section towards the middle of the book that I felt was slow and unnecessary. It’s not that I didn’t enjoy it; I just felt that the book was moving at a pretty good pace and then Harris slammed on the breaks. <br /><br />The characters are amazing in this book. Of course Clarice and Lecter stand out because the book is really about them, but Harris wrote several characters that were so evil I couldn’t stand them. I cheered when certain of those characters met their end and didn’t blink an eye at the horrible way in which they were dispatched. The other big plus for this book when it comes to Lecter is the fact he is front and center in this book. In the previous two books he is more of a background character. Even being a background character, Lecter is still one of the most terrifying and fascinating villains I have read. Having a book dedicated entirely to Lecter allowed Harris to flesh out the character more and terrify us in all new ways. Don’t mistake me, this isn’t a horror novel or scary like IT, but the actions of Lecter and several other characters is so intense I was chilled to think that there are people in our world who think like this. <br /><br />We also get to see a whole new side to Clarice. In the very start of the book she is tasked with a very difficult operation for the FBI and when it doesn’t go as planned the Tattler is there to smear her all over the rag of a paper. She is troubled by the way she is being viewed by the public and her job at the FBI comes into question. Harris uses this to show her gaining great strength as she progresses through this story. <br /><br />It appears I had more to say than I thought. I really enjoyed this book and even though I had heard this book was the worst of the series, to me I would say it is really a close second to Red Dragon. I can’t wait to see what Harris has in store for us next.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1587387201080630965">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_804635582">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/804635582" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6680101-sage" class="left imgcol" title="Sage"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1354339334p2/6680101.jpg" alt="Sage" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/804635582?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 19, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6680101-sage" class="user" title="Sage">Sage</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer804635582">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6028966078099836117">Fans of the first two Hannibal novels (including me) might need to adjust their expectations before reading this third installation: it has absolutely no suspense. It seemed as if Thomas Harris' writing style changed completely. There were scenes that could have been better if written differently. I'm a sucker for anything emotionally demanding, and this was the complete opposite of that. But did the stoic writing make this a bad book? Certainly, not.<br /><br />Much like Hannibal Lecter, this book is not e</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6028966078099836117">Fans of the first two Hannibal novels (including me) might need to adjust their expectations before reading this third installation: it has absolutely no suspense. It seemed as if Thomas Harris' writing style changed completely. There were scenes that could have been better if written differently. I'm a sucker for anything emotionally demanding, and this was the complete opposite of that. But did the stoic writing make this a bad book? Certainly, not.<br /><br />Much like Hannibal Lecter, this book is not emotionally driven. Rather it is sublime. It is clever. The characters are all just playing mind games with each other <em> and </em> the reader. They are all rotten in their own peculiar way. I especially enjoyed how Harris presented Paul Krendler and exposed his pathetic entity, but in a subtle way. Jack Crawford was shown, decayed, in his last years of usefulness in the FBI. Mason Verger's psychopathy and power was distressfully interesting. Clarice Starling is brought back as a significant character. and Hannibal Lecter, with all his charming qualities and preferences, and occasional tendencies to kill, is just <em> divine </em>.<br /><br />It felt like a patchy book, but it was well-researched and just clever. I can't think of a better word for it.<br /><br />I love you Thomas Harris.<br /><br />4 stars.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6028966078099836117">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_78970243">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/78970243" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/1324724-laura" class="left imgcol" title="Laura"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1282519794p2/1324724.jpg" alt="Laura" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/78970243?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Nov 30, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1324724-laura" class="user" title="Laura">Laura</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer78970243">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13070022571568035782">I am absolutely heartbroken that I've finished this series! I have overly optimistic hopes that Thomas Harris will surprise everyone with another addition, but I doubt that I'll be that lucky.<br />I've read a lot of reviews which have said that Hannibal is far worse than any of the other books, and that the ending (different from the film's) is too unrealistic to believe. I have to disagree with them all!<br />I loved this book, and even though it's been 2 days since I finished it, I've read and re-read th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13070022571568035782">I am absolutely heartbroken that I've finished this series! I have overly optimistic hopes that Thomas Harris will surprise everyone with another addition, but I doubt that I'll be that lucky.<br />I've read a lot of reviews which have said that Hannibal is far worse than any of the other books, and that the ending (different from the film's) is too unrealistic to believe. I have to disagree with them all!<br />I loved this book, and even though it's been 2 days since I finished it, I've read and re-read the final few chapters far too many times than is probably healthy; and I still can't stop Hannibal and Clarice from twirling through my head. The ending is a little far-fetched, but to my mind, completely perfect. It is the ending the series HAD to have, and written perfectly - in that I would quite happily beg Thomas Harris, in person, to continue on a 'what-happened-next' basis in a new book. Because I need to know!<br />Very, very rarely is a character designed and brought to life on a page quite so perfectly as Hannibal is in this book, and every aspect of his personality is explored so thoroughly in both Hannibal and Hannibal Rising, that it is almost quite difficult to believe he is a mere work of fiction.<br />Obviously, I recommend this book unreservedly. But reading Hannibal Rising first gives it added clarity. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13070022571568035782">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1409860284">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1409860284" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/19169870-scarlet" class="left imgcol" title="Scarlet"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1451105246p2/19169870.jpg" alt="Scarlet" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1409860284?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 06, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/19169870-scarlet" class="user" title="Scarlet">Scarlet</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/5577412-hannibal" title="Hardcover 9788425334115" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1409860284">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1214943318259561829">Este libro nos presenta por primera vez a un Hannibal humano, no como un ente físico superior a cualquiera que se le presente. Lecter debe usar <u>parte</u> de sus recursos para poder liberarse de una situación de vida o muerte, pero esto no es lo que lo humaniza, sino su relación con Clarice, su interaccion y obsesión con ella. Finalmente entendemos el porque de esta fascinación de Lecter con la policia y vemos a Starling levantarse al nivel Hannibal.<br /><br />La historia la llevan los personajes, sabemos que t</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText1214943318259561829">Este libro nos presenta por primera vez a un Hannibal humano, no como un ente físico superior a cualquiera que se le presente. Lecter debe usar <u>parte</u> de sus recursos para poder liberarse de una situación de vida o muerte, pero esto no es lo que lo humaniza, sino su relación con Clarice, su interaccion y obsesión con ella. Finalmente entendemos el porque de esta fascinación de Lecter con la policia y vemos a Starling levantarse al nivel Hannibal.<br /><br />La historia la llevan los personajes, sabemos que tan fuerte puede ser la obsesión de un hombre, y como poder luchar con o contra ella.<br /><br />El final...muchisimo mejor que el de la película. Logro convertir a Hannibal en uno de los personaje más perturvardoramente encantadores que he conocido, pero esta apertura a su historia fue lo que lo coronó.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="1214943318259561829">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
