<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_630281539">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/630281539" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2772745-kim" class="left imgcol" title="Kim"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1328013581p2/2772745.jpg" alt="Kim" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/630281539?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 05, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2772745-kim" class="user" title="Kim">Kim</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2772745-kim?shelf=general-fiction" class="actionLinkLite">general-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer630281539">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13906635233305020423">This is not a crime novel. It's certainly set up like one, yes, but it's much more than that. Hannibal is not only a book that revolves around a killer and his unusual relationship with an FBI Agent - it's a close examination of good versus evil, innocence versus corruption, and most of all, the evils of institutionalized misogyny and how the people we think we are supposed to trust betray us in the most harmful and damaging ways. It's both a horror story and a psychological thriller wrapped up</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13906635233305020423">This is not a crime novel. It's certainly set up like one, yes, but it's much more than that. Hannibal is not only a book that revolves around a killer and his unusual relationship with an FBI Agent - it's a close examination of good versus evil, innocence versus corruption, and most of all, the evils of institutionalized misogyny and how the people we think we are supposed to trust betray us in the most harmful and damaging ways. It's both a horror story and a psychological thriller wrapped up loosely in a murder saga.<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span style="display: none" class="spoilerContainer">[<br /><br />Those who say that Clarice Starling's character changed too much in this book are missing the point. First of all, Clarice begins the novel not as a wide-eyed, earnest rookie, but after seven bitter years of being mistreated and trampled upon by her superiors and increasingly growing bitter about the opportunities denied to her. Her career has not gone the way it should have because of jealous men and constant sexual harassment at work. Hell, seven years working for the FBI would be enough to change anyone, even without all of that. <br /><br />Thomas Harris is hyper aware of the misogyny that a woman like Clarice would have faced working within such a male dominated environment and he lets the reader know every step of the way. Paul Krendler is a glaring example of this. He seems to be, after Mason Verger, the most despicable person in the book. It is not Hannibal who broke Clarice in the end, or who caused her to utterly change her moral wiring. It was Krendler and the men in the FBI. By the time she broke into the barn to rescue Hannibal, she was already 'not herself'. From the moment she started killing men to save the person she originally set out to capture and give up to the FBI to be incarcerated, Clarice had already chosen her path. Quite simply, she had had enough. The FBI didn't want her? Didn't trust her? Even when she kept on persevering until the very end? Fine - if they wanted her to be bad so much, then she'd BE bad. And fuck 'em all. And not in the way they'd have wanted.<br /><br />This novel brutally shows us the very worst of humanity and not only in Hannibal himself. Throughout their corruption, their sexism and their mistreatment of one of their most moral and steadfast agents, the FBI lost someone very good to someone very evil. Had Krendler not been so intent on destroying Starling, had Crawford not chosen to distance himself so much from her, had the FBI only reinstated her temporarily once she notified them immediately of Hannibal's whereabouts and capture, Clarice's faith in humanity might have been restored somewhat and she would have been able to gather the moral shards within her soul and re-piece them together. But, denied all of this, she is only left to her thoughts, which eventually land upon the only person left who really seems to recognise and appreciate her, albeit in his own twisted way - Hannibal Lecter.<br /><br />It's a sad, twisted, gripping ending - Hannibal and Clarice share a taut relationship, with each one of them holding their breath, both having conditioned each other into forgetting their past traumas hoping that like this they would be able to function like normal human beings in a normal relationship. But it's an ending that works for such a dark story. And personally, I wouldn't have had it any other way.<br /><br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--><!--["br"]--></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13906635233305020423">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_112579393">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/112579393" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3658517-diane" class="left imgcol" title="Diane"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1340915558p2/3658517.jpg" alt="Diane" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/112579393?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 26, 2010</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3658517-diane" class="user" title="Diane">Diane</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer112579393">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14385283993049082971">This book is quite possibly what would be considered a disaster. There was never a single moment where I was enthralled enough to keep turning the pages. Of course, that's unfortunate, because it's set in a world where a monster like Hannibal Lecter runs free. The very earth should be shivering beneath his footfalls and it doesn't. Each page should be something of a continued suspension and I had no problems putting the book down to turn to something more important.<br /><br />I've always enjoyed the simpli</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14385283993049082971">This book is quite possibly what would be considered a disaster. There was never a single moment where I was enthralled enough to keep turning the pages. Of course, that's unfortunate, because it's set in a world where a monster like Hannibal Lecter runs free. The very earth should be shivering beneath his footfalls and it doesn't. Each page should be something of a continued suspension and I had no problems putting the book down to turn to something more important.<br /><br />I've always enjoyed the simplicity of style that Thomas Harris uses in his books. He never quite tells you exactly what goes on in his story and it leaves the reader groping for more and inclining their own minds to finish reduced scenes. This time, however, it was just irritating. I think if Dr. Lecter was a real man he would have been upset that his story was told in so much reduced form, as if nothing holds any meaning.<br /><br />The characters, which held up the story meekly, were as lame as a broken leg. Like many of Harris' novels surrounding Dr. Lecter, we find two villains. The more sinister, genius, cannibal and the mysterious criminals that are somehow connected to him in some way, as if his poisonous abilities have slipped out in the world to continue his dirty work in a rather poor fashion. Mason Verger is our second criminal. Half mad, half eaten, half dead. He is far from sinister. Though he has no obligations to the world and is under a delusional, religious, cleansing frenzy he is as weak as the respirator that gives him breath. Margot, his body building sister, is more malevolent and she turns out to be more brutal but she hardly gets enough page time, except for cracking nuts in her hand, to really get fearful of.<br /><br />Speaking of the Verger clan, Barney gets mixed up with them at one point and his entire stay in this book might as well have been the bumbling fool, in a scholar's clothing, who is just taking up space. He's obsessed with Dr. Lecter and yet he helps to bring him to a connived sense of justice in Mason's mind. Then he floats out of the book again only to appear later under the gun barrel of Ardelia, who is as useless as Crawford (simply acting as a removed security blanket for Starling), and then later when the novel ends.<br /><br />Getting to more substantial characters. Clarice Starling is 32 going on 33 years of age and she is much smarter, more efficient, but the same delicate little flower that she hides so well. She has also not climbed the ladder of judiciary action since we last saw her. Her humiliation attracts Dr. Lecter and in more ways than one. The novel's end is the most ridiculous thing I've probably ever read. It was as if, during the last forty pages, Harris had no idea how to conclude their little communication together so he gave into the carnal desires of lust and devotion and obsession. Clarice has never struck me as a woman who would annex her mind so easily, even if the mind is capable of creating an almost entirely new schema over a previous one. I feel I have already given too much away, if you're ever interested in reading this thing...though I suggest you do not.<br /><br />The one thing I liked about the continued character of Dr. Hannibal Lecter is that we start to get his own background. Now that he is a free agent we get into his brain much more often and though it is a beautifully wicked place to be in it is also full of reasons, just like anyone would have, for the way he is. We even see him weak, screaming laments for his past. It sets up the next book, Hannibal Rising, rather nicely with the presentation of his sister Mischa. Though he is our typically creepy Dr. Lecter he suddenly has this sensitive side at the end that makes me, once again, question Harris' reasoning for giving into carnality instead of a more practiced, thought out approach.<br /><br />All in all the book is hardly worth reading unless, unfortunately, you would like to continue to the next book or at least complete your own developed concepts of the Lecter saga. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14385283993049082971">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_480955635">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/480955635" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/5116650-janie-johnson" class="left imgcol" title="Janie Johnson"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1444996843p2/5116650.jpg" alt="Janie Johnson" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/480955635?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 15, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/5116650-janie-johnson" class="user" title="Janie Johnson">Janie Johnson</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/5116650-janie-johnson?shelf=2013-challenge" class="actionLinkLite">2013-challenge</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer480955635">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4501693037675940911">I have to say I really did enjoy this book even though so many have voiced their dislike of this one the most. I must place it between Red Dragon and Silence of the Lambs. Maybe because Lecter was more in the limelight in this installment of the series. We got to see the build up to Lecter's presence in this story. I enjoyed that. The story drew me in right from the start as the others before it did. <br /><br />Harris has such a very poetic writing style that I can't help but enjoy it. The words seem to fl</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4501693037675940911">I have to say I really did enjoy this book even though so many have voiced their dislike of this one the most. I must place it between Red Dragon and Silence of the Lambs. Maybe because Lecter was more in the limelight in this installment of the series. We got to see the build up to Lecter's presence in this story. I enjoyed that. The story drew me in right from the start as the others before it did. <br /><br />Harris has such a very poetic writing style that I can't help but enjoy it. The words seem to flow easily for him. In each of the books he writes his characters brilliantly. The ones you love and the ones you love to hate. All of them are pretty memorable to me. It was like I was allowed to crawl inside there heads and have a front row seat. IMO, Clarice is one of the stronger characters I have read in the line of detective/agent. And Lecter is perhaps one of the greatest villains ever brought to life. <br /><br />Reading about Lecter can be pretty disturbing. Just knowing that he could walk among many people and not be noticed while he was there. But in an odd way Harris makes him almost seem a hero in this one. I am not sure how I feel about that, but it is definitely not an expected feeling. I guess maybe because so many of the characters lived such twisted lives. I think some of them could even outdo Lecter.<br /><br />There are a couple of slow spots, but it really did not take away from the story for me. I enjoyed it page for page. Traveling the world with Lecter, what could be better? The further I went the less I could put it down. I gotta say The ending is not what I expected at all. And is probably what keeps me from a 5 star rating. No, it's not that it is a bad ending, it was actually pretty creative, it's just not one I wanted to see.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4501693037675940911">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_58179445">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/58179445" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/228975-daniel" class="left imgcol" title="Daniel"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" alt="Daniel" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/58179445?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jun 02, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/228975-daniel" class="user" title="Daniel">Daniel</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer58179445">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17153383890960888072">What the....?<br /><br />If when I was 400 pages into this read you asked me who I'd rate it, I would have replied that while it is a pretty sellar read it is definetely the weakest of Harris' Hannibal novels. Now that I've finished it I would dare mention that not only is it the weakest book Harris has written, but if there is a worse ending to a written work I haven't read it. <br /><br />Unlike Red Dragon or Silence of the Lambs, Hannibal is written like a supernatural thriller. Red Dragon and Buffalo Bill were both</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17153383890960888072">What the....?<br /><br />If when I was 400 pages into this read you asked me who I'd rate it, I would have replied that while it is a pretty sellar read it is definetely the weakest of Harris' Hannibal novels. Now that I've finished it I would dare mention that not only is it the weakest book Harris has written, but if there is a worse ending to a written work I haven't read it. <br /><br />Unlike Red Dragon or Silence of the Lambs, Hannibal is written like a supernatural thriller. Red Dragon and Buffalo Bill were both serial killers who had weaknesses and eventually got caught. But in this chapter of Lecter's life we are treated to a villain who has been elevated way beyond your typical killer. He doesn't feel pain, he can't be caught, he's smarter than everyone.... and the ending? Harris should be ashamed for this ending, in my most humble opinion. <br /><br />I won't give the ending away, but it is such a dramatic departure from the tone of the previous books that it necessitates a complete reversal in how they should be read. The books should no longer be read as psychological thrillers, but as supernatural thrillers. Lecter is portrayed as something other than human, so beyond everyone else that it stretches credibility. <br /><br />This will leave a bad taste in my mouth for a long time.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17153383890960888072">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_179142276">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/179142276" itemprop="url" />

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/179142276?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 17, 2014</a>

      <a href="/user/show/704900-lex" class="user" title="Lex">Lex</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="did not like it">did not like it</span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="did not like it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/704900-lex?shelf=horror-thriller" class="actionLinkLite">horror-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer179142276">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6170332859394011484">Let me start out by saying that I loved "The Silence of the Lambs" more than I ever expected to. The characters were engaging and multifaceted, the story was riveting, and the suspense built at a perfect pace. Starling was a rookie and in some ways naive, but she was a powerful female lead, an excellent foil to the charming but nefarious Dr. Lecter.<br /><br />Now take out everything likable about "Silence of the Lambs" and you have "Hannibal." I don't think words can do justice to just how distasteful I fo</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText6170332859394011484">Let me start out by saying that I loved "The Silence of the Lambs" more than I ever expected to. The characters were engaging and multifaceted, the story was riveting, and the suspense built at a perfect pace. Starling was a rookie and in some ways naive, but she was a powerful female lead, an excellent foil to the charming but nefarious Dr. Lecter.<br /><br />Now take out everything likable about "Silence of the Lambs" and you have "Hannibal." I don't think words can do justice to just how distasteful I found this book - and I'm not referring to the subject matter (if I was squeamish, I wouldn't have cared for "Silence of the Lambs,"after all). The characters became one-dimensional and Starling was re-written as a weak, pitiful, woman. Hypnotism a-la Hollywood (i.e. someone can be brainwashed overnight with no real memory of their previous life) is a reality. It's a shame because the idea of a survivor of one of Dr. Lecter's attacks seeking revenge upon his attacker seemed to be a potentially stellar plot line, but it really just fell through. This book falls profoundly short of what it could have been, and given the caliber of its predecessor, one know the author was capable of giving us something much better. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="6170332859394011484">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_162783543">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/162783543" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2747498-arun-divakar" class="left imgcol" title="Arun Divakar"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1253201408p2/2747498.jpg" alt="Arun Divakar" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/162783543?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 26, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2747498-arun-divakar" class="user" title="Arun Divakar">Arun Divakar</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer162783543">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14677421605486005661">Question: Why does Hannibal Lecter command a cult following ? What is different in him from a Ted Bundy or a Charles Manson ? The answer : general awesomeness !! Lecter is one of the most appalling, brilliant,classy, terrifying, ruthless ( and countless other such terms) characters in popular fiction of our time. Thomas Harris in one of those rare interviews called Lecter 'The dark side of our world'. <br /><br />I will draw comparisons to a stringed instrument here : <em> Silence of the lambs </em> was about you se</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14677421605486005661">Question: Why does Hannibal Lecter command a cult following ? What is different in him from a Ted Bundy or a Charles Manson ? The answer : general awesomeness !! Lecter is one of the most appalling, brilliant,classy, terrifying, ruthless ( and countless other such terms) characters in popular fiction of our time. Thomas Harris in one of those rare interviews called Lecter 'The dark side of our world'. <br /><br />I will draw comparisons to a stringed instrument here : <em> Silence of the lambs </em> was about you seeing the instrument for the first time. Someone showed you the instrument for the first time out of its casing, explained its history to you and slowly you begin the process of tuning it. Towards the end of the novel you have music flowing uninterrupted and you feel it coursing through the air around you. <em> Hannibal </em> opens with those resonant chords still vibrating in the air around you and takes you on journeys which you sometime feel are roads you have taken before. This notwithstanding the first half is quite wonderful to read. However as the fate of all good things, this symphony comes to an end. The over tuned instrument finally suffers a broken string throwing melody to the gutter holes of disharmony. The ending is quite a washout in the tale and I did not warm up to it. This was the only speck of dust (albeit large) in an otherwise pristine sheet of plot. <br /><br />Thomas Harris has created a larger-than-life anti-hero in a brilliant way. It has influenced popular culture in tremendous ways as well. A search on google gave me atleast four to five returns in a single page doing a character dissection and even a psycho analysis of this fictional fiend. It is a master stroke from the author to have created a serial killer with cannibalistic shades and snobbish tastes(whoever would have thought up a genius who works on astrophysics and particle physics based on the assumptions made by Stephen Hawking after a string of murders ? That too after playing <em> Goldberg Variations </em> on a harpsichord while driving around in a Bentley !!).<br /><br />There is only so far that you can stretch an elastic band, beyond it the band will break.It's the same with novels, sometimes familiarity sows the seeds of contempt which may then be reaped in a sequel to come. <em>Hannibal Rising </em> was the same stringed instrument after it had been run over by a steam roller !!!<br /><br />Recommended.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14677421605486005661">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <a href="/user/show/1441594-charlotte" class="left imgcol" title="Charlotte"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1219188355p2/1441594.jpg" alt="Charlotte" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/56472049?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 18, 2009</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1441594-charlotte" class="user" title="Charlotte">Charlotte</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok">it was ok</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="it was ok"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer56472049">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7644001401511165759">Dr. Lecter has not been as careful as he should have been, and is now hunted both by the FBI and a revengeful sadist. Clarice Starling has not been as careful as she should have been, and is now at the mercy of both resentful FBI colleagues and the aforementioned sadist. [Anguished tone:] How ever will they escape?<br /><br />Why, through some major plot hole, of course! Incoherence plagues the book (characterization is particularly lame, and the ending tragically silly), as do too many verb-less sentences.</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7644001401511165759">Dr. Lecter has not been as careful as he should have been, and is now hunted both by the FBI and a revengeful sadist. Clarice Starling has not been as careful as she should have been, and is now at the mercy of both resentful FBI colleagues and the aforementioned sadist. [Anguished tone:] How ever will they escape?<br /><br />Why, through some major plot hole, of course! Incoherence plagues the book (characterization is particularly lame, and the ending tragically silly), as do too many verb-less sentences. Had I had to go through one more chapter opening with a participial phrase trying to pass itself of as a sentence, I might have had to write an official letter of complaint to Mr. Thomas.<br /><br />To top it all (and this is a personal stance), I tend to resent art who try to get you to root for the decidedly bad. Somehow, the sociopath Lecter should be redeemed because he has good taste in Bordeaux and a child-sadistic nemesis: blah. So what else do we have as a justification: killer pigs? Childhood trauma? Exquisite cooking skills? Blah blah blah.<br /><br />The result: I wanted this book to be over so much, I had trouble putting it down. Outrageous details (hormones-inflated lesbians, tear martinis, the afore-mentioned killer pigs, etc.) helped a little before they turned boring; the occasional flash of good writing (esp. descriptions) made this readable.<br /><br />But blah. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7644001401511165759">...more</a>

          </span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_225752948">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/225752948" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/6482860-kylie" class="left imgcol" title="Kylie"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1319154260p2/6482860.jpg" alt="Kylie" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/225752948?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Oct 20, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/6482860-kylie" class="user" title="Kylie">Kylie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/32418.Hannibal" title="Paperback 9780099297703" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer225752948">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17794145672411730456">A very creepy series, great to read over Halloween. The first book, The Red Dragon, I have yet to read because I refuse to. I saw the movie, and I didn't enjoy the plot. You can absolutely read the other three books without ever reading the first. The fourth book, Hannibal Rising, described the life of Hannibal Lector as a child and the horrors he endured. The Silence of the Lambs and Hannibal are absolutely fantastic and I wish he had made more of Dr. Hannibal Lector's life known after living i</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17794145672411730456">A very creepy series, great to read over Halloween. The first book, The Red Dragon, I have yet to read because I refuse to. I saw the movie, and I didn't enjoy the plot. You can absolutely read the other three books without ever reading the first. The fourth book, Hannibal Rising, described the life of Hannibal Lector as a child and the horrors he endured. The Silence of the Lambs and Hannibal are absolutely fantastic and I wish he had made more of Dr. Hannibal Lector's life known after living in Europe. <br />This book, Hannibal, is the third of the series. I gave the rating a four because the ending was disappointing. The movie's interpretation of the book was horrible. The ending was nothing like the book, probably because the book's ending wasn't all that interesting either. In the ending of the movie, Hannibal escaped the law with a missing hand and a first and last goodbye's kiss to Clarice. However, the book's ending consisted of Clarice and Hannibal marrying and running off to a country in Europe and becoming a very wealthy couple. I refuse to believe either ending happened, and I wish Thomas Harris had thought more on the ending for readers like me! </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17794145672411730456">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {

    }
  }

  }

Allen&lt;\/a&gt;\n      &lt;\/div&gt;\n\n          &lt;div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\"&gt;\n            &lt;span class=\"minirating\"&gt;&lt;span class=\"stars staticStars\"&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p6\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p0\"&gt;&lt;\/span&gt;&lt;\/span&gt; 3.80 avg rating &amp;mdash; 363 ratings&lt;\/span&gt;            &amp;mdash; published 1993\n          &lt;\/div&gt;\n\n    &lt;div class=\"addBookTipDescription\"&gt;\n      \n&lt;span id=\"freeTextContainer12951871519740093944\"&gt;\"The Exorcist\", a 1973 movie about a twelve-year-old girl possessed by the Devil, frightened people more than any horror film ever did. Many moviegoers sought therapy to rid themselves of fears they could not explain. Psychiatrists coined the term \"c&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;span id=\"freeText12951871519740093944\" style=\"display:none\"&gt;&amp;quot;The Exorcist&amp;quot;, a 1973 movie about a twelve-year-old girl possessed by the Devil, frightened people more than any horror film ever did. Many moviegoers sought therapy to rid themselves of fears they could not explain. Psychiatrists coined the term &amp;quot;cinematic neurosis&amp;quot; for patients who left the movie feeling a terrifying presence of demons. At the Washington premiere, a young woman stood outside the theater, trembling. &amp;quot;I come out here in the sunlight,&amp;quot; she said, &amp;quot;and I see people\'s eyes, and they frighten me.&amp;quot;Among the few moviegoers unmoved by the horror were two priests, Father William S. Bowdern and Father Walter Halloran, members of the Jesuit community at St. Louis University. &amp;quot;Billy came out shaking his head about the little girl bouncing on the bed and urinating on the crucifix,&amp;quot; Halloran remembers. &amp;quot;He was kind of angry. \'There is a good message that can be given by this thing,\' he said. The message was the fact that evil spirits operate in our world.&amp;quot;Bowdern and Halloran knew that the movie was fictional veneer masking a terrible reality. Night after night in March and April 1949, Bowdern had been an exorcist, with Halloran assisting. Bowdern fervently believed that he had driven a demon from a tormented soul. The victim had been a thirteen-year-old boy strangely lured to St. Louis from a Maryland suburb of Washington. Bowdern\'s exorcism had been the inspiration for the movie.The true story of this possession, told in Possessed, is based on a diary kept by a Jesuit priest assisting Father Bowdern. The diary, the most complete account of an exorcism since the Middle Ages, is published for the first time in this revised edition of Possessed.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/12455.Thomas_Harris">About Thomas Harris</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/12455.Thomas_Harris"><img alt="12455" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1194544741p2/12455.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer9538564745960190450">Thomas Harris began his writing career covering crime in the United States and Mexico, and was a reporter and editor for the Associated Press in New York City. His first novel, <em>Black Sunday</em>, was printed in 1975, followed by <em>Red Dragon</em> in 1981, <em>The Silence of the Lambs</em> in 1988, <em>Hannibal</em> in 1999, and <em>Hannibal Rising</em> in 2006.</span>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/12455.Thomas_Harris" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Thomas Harris...</a>
<div class="clear"></div></div></div><div class="bigBoxBottom"></div></div>
